et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	and empty the matter that is inside, and apply to the place medicine that discharges putrefaction for some days, then treat it as you would an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And sometimes this vein branches off, especially when it appears at the joint of the foot, or in the foot, and there is much perforation, and thus it often bleeds;
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	Treat it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that are born between the skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This disease is called in our land "the buffalo disease," because it often occurs among buffaloes, and it is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh, and travels throughout the body moving up and down, and one can feel it well as it moves from limb to limb, until it breaks the skin where it goes, and causes pain.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is caused by putrefaction of certain humors, such as worms and snakes and maggots in the intestines;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	and be wary of its malicious nature, for when it travels through the body, and ascends to the head, and reaches the eye, it may by chance enter, and destroy the eye;
et ceu avient maintes fois.	and this happens often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see the need to cure and drain it, one must not delay once it has spread:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	then it is necessary to bind the area above and below with a strong and tight bandage, then cut into it and drain it forcefully, and if the pus is deeply embedded in the flesh, and you cannot find it, cauterize the area with fire until it subsides;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm it causes is that it can corrupt the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming near the head close to the eye, then firmly grasp the eyebrow area, then cut above it, and draw out the fire.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and the patient should use cleansing of the body with soluble medicines for purging bad humors, and avoid foods that cause putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to certain limbs, and can move from one limb to another;
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and I saw what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to see a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm;
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	And immediately after, the flesh rises like a worm on the shoulder, faster than anything, like quicksilver when it is cut from its place;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	the pain leaves that place and fixes itself in the shoulder, and then a little while later runs throughout the entire body until it reaches the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that it quickly circled around her body, as I saw it happen.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly at how it moved from limb to limb, for I had never seen this disease behave in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	Still, I had heard of many who wished to move pain from one place to another, but I had not seen it myself as I did in this woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and I thought it was because the woman had a dry body and her veins exposed, which made this windiness constrained;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	And they do not perceive according to this reasoning for those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and veins that lie flat.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you wish to treat this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears as we have said, then place it above and below quickly, and then incise until that windiness constricts at its site;
et cauterize le leu;	and cauterize the site;
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you do not see it with your own eyes, then treat it as one would an accumulation of wind, such as with pungent pills, and snake skin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows vary according to their appearances and the parts of the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity among them is such that there are those with large points, and small ones, and hairy, and smooth.
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and of those which have two angles, and of those which have tongues, and of those where there are pieces;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and when it falls on any limb, it falls in two ways:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	where it falls on a principal limb, such as the brain, heart, liver, spleen, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar limbs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls then in any part of these limbs, and the signs of death, which I will tell you next, become apparent:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	you should be wary of extracting this arrow, for death follows in many cases;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when these bad signs do not appear, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then remove it and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the signs of the brain when an arrow falls and pierces the bone, and jumps the meninges which are over the brain, are when scotoma and headache and vertigo and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of tongue, and spasm and disturbance of understanding, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and sometimes it passes without meninges from the nostrils, or from the ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and sometimes speech and voice are lost;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and from the wound moisture white like milk comes out, and it also flows like pus;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if these signs appear to you, then proceed with the treatment, and draw out the arrow if it is inside.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of an arrow when it falls in the heart is that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and sometimes the arrow moves like hair, and black blood comes out, and coldness and cold sweat occur, and syncope sets in:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	then you can be sure that death will follow shortly.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that pierces the windpipe is that white foam spurts from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and sighs loudly and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrow falls in the covering of the hip, it is near the small ribs;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and causes great pain and groaning and sighing;
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and the movement affects all the shoulder limbs.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow strikes in the stomach, perhaps some undigested flesh will spurt from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow strikes in the abdomen, and no piece of it can be felt through any part of the intestines, there is no hope for treatment or for extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine jumps out and comes pouring forth, and the patient feels great pain:
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, such as the face and neck and throat and shoulder and arm pit and spine of the back and ribs and thigh and legs, and similar limbs, are safe according to many conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you that it happened to me, for this reason do as I say.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a man that an arrow fell in his skull at the root of his nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and I extracted it from the other side behind the ear, and he was healthy without further issue.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And I extracted an arrow that fell into the fatty tissue under the eyelid above the eyeball, and the arrow was buried, and little could be reached except for the tip towards the shaft, and the arrow was large from a Turkish bow, entirely of light iron without feathers;
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	The joint was sound, and no bad accidents occurred.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And he extracted an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabian with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I grasped the barbs, and was subtle enough to extract it, and the Christian was saved.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I extracted an arrow from a man who had it embedded in his stomach, and I thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and after thirty days had passed, his condition did not change;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut around the arrow, and managed it skillfully, and forcefully extracted it, and he did not suffer any bad consequences.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you wish to treat a man who has an arrow embedded in his back, and the wound is sealed over;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and the arrow remains inside him, and he does not change his natural disposition in any way, nor finds harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And you wish to treat another man who has an arrow shot into his face, and the wound is sealed over;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and it remains thus without him suffering great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And treat an arrow in the head of one of the king's princes, which was embedded between his ears, and it was slightly inclined to the right side;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	And the arrow was completely buried.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called to treat her three days after she fell ill.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I examined her thoroughly and found nothing.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and she felt pain and discomfort behind her right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I applied a poultice to the area to prevent swelling;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and the location of the arrow became apparent.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I applied the poultice for several more days, and reopened the wound, and the patient remained like this for a long time, until he felt the arrow inside his nose for one day;
et il le me dist.	and he tells him to do it.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I applied a corrosive medicinal agent to the wound for several days until it was open, and I probed it, feeling the head of the arrow that lay in place.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I inserted the corrosive medicine into the wound opening until the head of the arrow became visible.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and after about four months, I carefully enlarged the wound so that I could place the forceps inside, but it would not come out.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	then I continued to devise and craft various instruments until one day I was able to grasp it with well-made forceps, as described at the end of this chapter, and removed it, then treated the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the physician judges that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I then repaired it, and the wound was sealed, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	I have told you about the nature of extracting some arrows, so place your care on what I do not say, for books cannot encompass everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	but wise masters compare well with great things, and with what is present and lacking, they find new work, and new instruments, in the descent of strange things that occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows exit from the members in which they are embedded in two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	at the place where they enter, or from another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and when it jumps out where it entered, it is an arrow entering the flesh, and sometimes it may jump out immediately now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump out now, wait until the flesh around it is swollen and then ease the exit;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and if it is embedded in the bone and cannot come out, leave it for several days and soften it each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it will jump out; and if it does not, carefully cut around it with a sharp instrument until the area around it is enlarged, and then extract it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is embedded in the bone of the head and goes to one of the sides of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have mentioned become apparent to the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	do not remove it, but leave it as is for a few days, because if the arrow reaches the brain, it is fatal.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is embedded only in the bone and does not reach the surface, and the patient remains safe for several days without a bad outcome, then attempt to extract it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot be removed, administer cold applications around it, as I have told you;
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the area until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is lodged in the body where it cannot be seen, search for it throughout the entire body;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then draw it with some suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if you cannot due to the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone or nerve or vein, then cut as much as necessary so that the wound is large enough;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and draw out the arrow if you can, and if it has barbs that hold it in place, remove the flesh that is embedded from two sides as much as you can, and then break or bend the barbs so that you may pull it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and be careful that you do not break the arrow, as pulling it out would then be more difficult.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, leave it until the area around the site is healed, then pull it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the bleeding from the wound opposes you, then administer what we have said about its treatment in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	and beware of cutting the nerve and the vein, and proceed cautiously so that you can draw out the arrow without danger, whether quickly or slowly, firmly or gently;
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	and place the patient in the position he was in when the arrow struck him, for this is the greatest aid there can be, and if you cannot do so, then place him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another place, where it is apparent some part of it remains, or where the skin is swollen in such a way that it can be seen or felt clearly:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	Cut above, where the forceps can grasp, and then extract:
si saut fuer maintenant.	do it now with strength.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand around until it enters the bone, then expand the bone, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it be for now, and then restart the extraction until it comes out;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the shaft of the arrow is there, cut it off at the base;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if the shaft breaks off, and you wish to administer cautery, then apply the instrument cautiously so that the tip of the arrow penetrates into the blade of the instrument;
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and then cut forcefully, and if the arrow is embedded, apply the instrument with its tip entering in, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is contaminated, you must cut away all the flesh around where the venom is, if possible, then treat the wound as necessary.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow falls into the thigh or in the belly or at the bladder or in the groin, and it is close, and you can cut over it, do so;
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and be careful not to cut the vein and the nerve, then extract it, and then sew up the wound if necessary;
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and care for it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pliers used to treat arrows is like the beak of a bird, and see here the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are many ways to do this:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the hair awl is also like the feather of a bird, to pierce at the tip of the arrow, as shown here is the form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of the tongs for applying and holding is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	There are thirty-one veins from which one can bleed to health, sixteen of which are in the head, namely:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	The blows which are behind the ears, which are called the two "herbech";
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the two arteries which are in the two visible temples;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and the two veins which are in the sockets of the two eyes, which are called "aspires";
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein which is on the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein which is at the top of the nose;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two jugulars which are in the neck;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins which are on the upper lip, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich";
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two veins which are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins from which one usually bleeds are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic vein, and it is on the left side, and laypeople call it "vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	and the middle one is called "faste," and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins, and laypeople call it "vein of the heart";
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and the basilic vein is on the right side, and laypeople call it "vein of the belly," and it is near the fossa, and this is the one from which one usually bleeds, which appears clearly on the forearm.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the saphenous vein is the one between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg and foot there are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	one is near the curvature of the shin bone on the left side, and the second saphenous vein which is at the ankle of the right side;
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein called "nexus," which is at the ankle of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are three veins near those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The treatment of veins that are behind the ears helps with chronic catarrhs and migraine;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	And the qualities of the surgeon, as I tell you, are that he raises the head of the patient, and rubs the place where the veins are with a rough cloth;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	then bind the patient's neck with a bandage, so that the two veins appear behind the ears in two places dependent on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	feel them then with your finger, and where you feel the pulse below your finger, make an incision;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	then take the lancet, and insert it below the vein up to the bone, then raise your hand along the entire length of the vein, and cut through both the skin and the vein well two fingers wide, and let out as much blood as you wish;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then strain and bind it until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already mentioned the incision and the cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The treatment of the two arteries that are in the two temples is worth for chronic migraine, and severe headache, and habitual ophthalmic conditions, and for the continuous flow of tears from the eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of the practitioner are as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	and the patient should squeeze his neck until the two veins become distinctly visible;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feel the pulse below your thumb, and then cut into it;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	Then lift the heart above the vein towards your thumb index, and insert the lancet beneath, lift the vein upwards, and cut it, just as you did with the other two veins, and let the blood flow according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then loosen the patient and place your finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then bind it tightly, and leave it until it is healed;
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and we have already spoken about their cutting and extraction, at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The vein of the forehead is worth as much as the cephalic vein for treating old face diseases, and for migraine, and redness;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality is such that the patient strains his neck by twisting it, until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument called "fossaor", of which here is its form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the tip on the vein, and press with your hand, or something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity you wish;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then release the patient's neck, and tie off the vein until it is secure, and sometimes the work is done with a flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	Nevertheless, it must not be that the flame is too sharp;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	and proceed carefully across, as the bone is close, and by chance the flame may break when it is fine.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The salve of the two veins that are in the two tear ducts helps the eyes, and for eyelid inflammation, and for redness in the eye, and for sties on the eyelash, and for diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of its application is that the patient should pull their neck with a twist using some kind of cloth, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then apply the salve, and let it be applied thinly, a little along the flame shape a little wide, because there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the flames are fine, they might break;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	then let the blood flow as much as you need, and then cover it with cloth, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The vein of the nose is beneficial for fever, and for furious diarrhea, and for diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes to the face, especially when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	and the qualities of the vein are such that the patient should squeeze their neck, then press their nose with your left hand, and take a fine flame long, and place it between the two nostrils, because the vein does not appear well otherwise, and the blood will now begin to flow;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your necessity, then bandage it for a night, for it heals very quickly;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The salve of the two binders helps in the constriction of the almaine, and at the beginning of mixing, and for many diseases, and for empetigo, and for corrosions, and for herpes, and for abscesses;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the properties of the salve are such that the patient constricts their neck below one and the other, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	and let the master stand over the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a chair, then open the vein on the long side slightly, then draw blood moderately, as much as is necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	Then do the same on the other vein, then loosen the bandage, and bind all the veins moderately so that the patient does not strangle;
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and leave it until morning, so that the wound may heal.
de la sainie des leivres	of the healing of wounds
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The healing of veins in the lips above helps with swelling in the mouth, and decay of gums, and splits in the lips, and nose, and around them.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the treatment is to have the patient sit before you, and bind his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	then turn the lip and examine the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, which can be recognized by their black color and by the small black veins around them:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	so then probe both veins, and if you do not know them and are in doubt, probe the larger one on each side, and do the same for the two veins above and below, because it is done in the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Remove the tonsil from the root
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The healing of the veins that are behind the tongue helps after the healing of the cephalic vein, and this is at the constriction of the throat, and in diseases of the eye, and in diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the qualities of the healer are such that the patient urinates into your hands in front of the sun, and he lifts his tongue, and you look underneath on each side for a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	treat then one and the other, but do not go too deep, for below are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins of the arm that are commonly treated are treated in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	either by cutting the entire arm with a sharp blade, or an olive wood scalpel like cutting knives, and it is called "anesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	And they are wide and subtle according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame of fire is very famous, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open veins that are full of thick, visible blood, and which contain thick and turbid blood;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtle and pointed, and is for bleeding fine veins, where there is fine yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that affect the throat, neck, chest, and abdomen;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the physician to bleed wisely and to avoid the artery which is behind.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and continuous bleeding occurs, he must stop it, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and must not prick the flame, but cut as before.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilica does not appear clearly, then you must extract it, and change to another one;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	where you want any vein of it, or heal in its place the vein on the arm:
elle apert manifestement;	it appears clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and the cup to the flame as before, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you want to know the place of the healing, then you must extract the arm, and touch the place until you feel the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	Then mark the place of the bone, and then bind the arm, and cut the vein on the forearm;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	and be careful not to hit the artery when you see the place swollen, for it is the artery:
eschui la donques.	avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it flowing upwards like a child's urine, and the blood is red and thin, know that this is arterial blood:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	hurry then, and place your finger firmly, then remove your finger if the bleeding stops, as this often happens;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	bind the arm, and leave it thus, and do not move the patient;
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be under fear, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if the wound is not staunched, and it is necessary, and the medicine is not present, then cut the artery if it opens, for the head will follow.
et estainche li sans.	and staunch the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take the bark of figs, and cut it, and take one of the halves and apply it well until the other day;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	if the wound is staunched, it is good;
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if not, then treat it as we have said, with powders that staunch blood;
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the stiffness is not severe in many positions due to the small area of the wound, and the strength of the arm's ligament.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The median vein in the middle helps to drain blood from the head above and the body below, as it is composed of the basilica and cephalic veins, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	And it is necessary for the surgeon to be cautious near the nerve that is below, and if he presses too deeply, and finds the nerve, it swells and the patient suffers greatly, and perhaps cannot be healed;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	And this nerve is often apparent, and if it does not appear in some people due to its subtlety, then you must handle it with a tranquilizing instrument;
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	And avoid the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then make the incision lengthwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The bloodletting of the cephalic vein helps to draw blood from the head and aids the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is necessary to bleed by puncturing with an olive blade or a myrtle blade, for this is the safest of all veins, as it has no nerves or arteries nearby.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Nevertheless, it is necessary to find the most gentle place, and do not worry if it is not possible the first time, and try again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And sometimes the area swells in some people when it is done for the first time, but it does not cause any harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the salve is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you must know about medicine is that it is not aimed except to preserve health and to avoid future diseases;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	and let the medicine be administered through one of the three veins that are in the arm:
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	that is to say, cephalic, facial, and basilic;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one should administer medicine at the beginning of spring, in autumn and winter after eating, when signs of fullness appear;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	and one should administer medicine on the first day or the third, after two hours or three of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The medicine administered for diseases has no fixed time, but should be given when needed, day or night, at any hour and in all seasons;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And it is not appropriate to bleed children until they are fourteen years old, nor women carrying a fetus from the fourth month until the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	And one should not treat the elderly who have surpassed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when someone wishes to be bled, in whatever manner it may be, it is necessary for them to cleanse their intestines with a mild enema if they have retained much feces, so that the veins do not attract from the intestines harmful excesses detrimental to the principal limbs;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	nor should one bleed those who are overly full of meat, nor drunkards, until they have sobered up, nor hydropics;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if one wishes to bleed after colic pain, and vomiting, and diarrhea, and frequent sexual activity, and labor, lack of sleep, and fasting, and anything that exhausts all the strength, whether from something in food or from the body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	Then subtly thin the humors, if the blood is thick, through food and drink and medicine, if you have the power to do so;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	Then enter the bath, if nothing prevents it, to thin the blood, and bleed from the vein around the elbow, as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and on that day, guard yourself from work, and from piercing, and from excess, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	and be tied and joyful, and let the patient lie higher than the person being bled, and rub the arm two or three times, then tighten the bandage moderately, for if it is too tight, the blood cannot flow.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the area with your hands until the veins swell and can be felt;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	then moisten the needle with a drop of old oil, then place the thumb of your left hand on the vein below the area where you wish to puncture it, so that the vein does not move when pricked.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that move like cords when the needle is applied, and some are full of air, so that when you place the needle, it recoils from the needle, and thus cannot be opened.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if the vein is too narrow, then it is necessary that the phlebotomist be cautious in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the vein acts for the first time, it is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	if not, then recommence again a bit below that place or above quickly, if the area is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the area is swollen and the patient is frightened, leave it for one or two days and do not bind the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	by chance, abscesses may come;
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	do not enter the bath, then restart the treatment if it pleases them;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the opening is small, cauterize the skin gently and if you doubt that it will not release as much blood as you wish, apply heat directly to that opening.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	and work quickly, so that the area does not swell;
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the area swollen, do not repeat the incision, and place a little poultice of oil on it, for it alleviates the body of blood, and the poultice is soothing in this place.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus apply the poultice of oil to each incision you make on the veins, to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	and this same poultice causes thistle and pain when it is applied to the area;
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	So carefully feel the pulse and divide it when it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if there comes a large abscess, which happens many times, especially when the force is not sufficient at the time of the vein opening being small, then hurry, and place on it a sponge moistened in warm water and vinegar for about an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the blood comes from the vein, and if a black or green discoloration remains at the site for several days, it does no harm;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you wish, place some substance of aloes or myrrh dissolved in juice of calamint, mastix, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And many times there is an abscess and swelling at the base of the thumb:
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	Place your hand on it, and if you find the spot soft upon pressing with your hand, then that swelling is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	Avoid placing any of the things we have mentioned, for by chance it could cut into an artery;
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	but apply the dry poultice to harden the area, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw from each the blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red;
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	and if you see it thick, let it continue until it becomes thin.
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	And if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And for one who is full and swollen, and needs to have blood drawn, make the incision wider, and let the veins be wide;
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and it is necessary to bleed them little and often, and this should be done by cutting across, not deep;
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this method of bleeding is safe from blood loss and nerve damage, and is better than long or wide incisions.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And for one whose body needs nourishment during bleeding, give moist bread in pomegranate juice;
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	If it is heated, let the blood flow three or four times. And if it has a cold complexion, before bleeding give him moist bread in syrup of musk, or aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and strongly scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints after the loss of much blood, it is necessary that he drinks broth of flesh, and fragrant syrup, and uses other things which we have said in the section or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to bleed his arm and let blood again, it is necessary, when he is weakened by much bleeding, that he lets blood a little at a time according to the quantity of his continuing strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wishes to bleed his arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong body, should let blood seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wishes to be bled from another place should do so on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For it has much blood within the body which is already heated, and causes fever;
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	so it is necessary to let out a large quantity of blood, and to widen the passage until it flows easily;
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	after you have considered all the conditions for bleeding, and place your hand on the pulse when bleeding, so that death does not occur due to carelessness, as this often happens when bleeders are negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	And it is not right when you wish to dislocate the arm, and let blood a second time, and the wound is closed, that you press firmly upon it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	nor if he is crooked, that he extend the arm quickly, for it would be worse;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	but leave it until it heals from the second time;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and you apply the tip of the flame, until the blood which has coagulated in the vein opening flows out, and put on a small poultice soaked in water, and press upon it lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it alone and do not bind it, until the abscess is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, do so from the same vein, or another vein, or from the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein on the arm is bled in place of the head vein because it is composed appropriately.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the method of healing is that the patient immerses his hand in hot water until the phlebitis becomes red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	Then bind moderately so that the vein is well compressed, now apply the salve across it, not along its breadth or length;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	And let the puncture be wide, and apply salves well near the joint of the hand, and if blood does not flow freely, then immerse the hand in warm water, and allow the blood to flow into the water until you have enough;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	And if it is winter, do not immerse the hand in warm water, for it is more appropriate to do so in summer than in winter;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the salve for this vein is safer than for all other veins, as there are no artery or nerve near it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The salivation of the right hand is worth for all diseases of the liver, and this is the manner:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	strain the hand, and put it in hot water until the veins swell, as one can see;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if the salivation goes sideways, and if you cover it entirely, then nothing will be harmed;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and do not go too deeply, for the nerves are completely bare of flesh, and then put the hand back in hot water if the salivation is frozen in the wound, and it cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn as much blood as is necessary, apply oil and thread to quickly close the vein, and do this for each incision.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The treatment of the left hand vein is effective for diseases of the spleen, and do it exactly as I have told you for the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The salve of the sophene is worth for all diseases that are below the body, such as disorders of the legs, and retention of urine, and disease of the thighs, and of the old hips, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the quality of this salivation is that the patient places their foot in hot water, and rubs on the vein until it bursts, and ties above the ankle joint;
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot there are many veins;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	treat then the widest vein, at the ankle, for it is worth more.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you treat it above the foot, be careful of the nerves that are below, and treat it across as if cutting through.
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and let the flame be extinguished.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, then reset the foot to its proper position, and let the vein be thoroughly opened.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the treatment fails the first time, then begin again slightly above it the second time, for the place is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	do not fear the nerve, as we have said, and do the same for the vein of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The site of the sciatic vein is at the ankle on the inside, and its incision relieves hip pain when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the qualities of its treatment are such that the patient enters the bath, and applies IV fingers above the ankle in twisting, because otherwise the vein does not appear.
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	and if it appears, then heal it in all ways that you can, and by crossing.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is better that you cut it, for the place is below, and it responds well to many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, then heal any line that appears on the back of the foot and near the little toe, and be careful of the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	and let the blood flow as much as you wish, and then loosen the ligature, and put on cotton and bind it;
ele est maintenant sanee.	She is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	cupping treatments
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Suction cups are made of horns, or wool, or glass;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	and suction is performed according to two methods:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	either by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this suction that does not involve striking is according to two methods:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	either it is done with heat, or without heat;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and the suction that is performed by striking and extracting blood is done at fourteen points on the body, of which one is entirely on the head;
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the other [dislocation] is in the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and two others on both sides of the neck;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the windpipe behind the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the windpipe of both shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the windpipe above the buttocks;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the windpipes within both arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the windpipes of both legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the windpipes of both ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and the windpipe treatment does not draw blood, except from small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and for this reason it does not weaken a person as does bleeding from a vein;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And it is not appropriate that it be treated, nor with any fire or sense of heat, in any illness that comes from overfullness, until the entire body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if due to the necessity of illness it is necessary to bleed, or by habit, we shall perform it every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and both in these times and throughout each period;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are those who, when they need to be bled, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are those who experience fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and neck, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, and are spitting blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are some who dream, and see in their sleep blood and wounds and deaths and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, especially in the middle of the month, we instruct them to bleed after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The treatment of the brain helps with the stiffness of the head... that affects the eyes, and it should not be done after the evacuation of the entire body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this ventilation is in place of the treatment of the head, and it is not suitable for those with a cold complexion to use, or who have catarrh, as it causes them great harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and for those reasons, it is not suitable for the elderly to use, nor for those who have cold diseases in their head;
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from it frequently become forgetful, and therefore it is necessary to place the cupping vessel a bit lower due to the risk of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	The ventosity is located at the nape of the neck and below the occipital bone, and for this reason it is useful for constriction of the stomach, and for splitting the channel of the groin, and for all purposes, and for distension;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and here it is necessary to apply pressure, because if it holds too tightly, it causes obstruction in the stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The ventosations at the second vertebra of the neck are useful for headaches, and for ophthalmic pain and migraine, and for choking, and for pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is located at the nape of the neck;
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and you should instruct the patient to press gently without pressing on the artery, and to avoid bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The ventilation below the chin is beneficial for mouth diseases, and for the corruption of gums, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth;
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and it is in the place of the sinuses below the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventosation of the shoulders is useful for diseases that come from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The ventilation of the axilla is as valuable as that of the three veins of the arm, for it draws blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the surgeon not to cut too deeply, for the area is bare of flesh, and it lies near nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The ventilation on the buttocks is effective for hemorrhoids of the anus and for diseases below it; the cup should be large and made of brass, requiring good suction.
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	and by chance, if they were delicate, they would break;
et i fai grans plaies.	and make large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The suction cups on the legs provide strong relief because they draw blood from the entire body, and they are effective for old pains in the thighs, and of the back, and of the bladder, and reset the flowers;
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and they are placed at the two shoulder joints, and the two ankles, and overall they weaken the body after long use, and cause fainting in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The method of applying the suction cup is to place it first empty, and then suck gently, and attach it quickly, and move it evenly, and do not stop doing this, until you see the area red and swollen, and feel the heat of the blood;
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	Then heat it, and apply cupping vessels, and be careful with the condition of the body, for there are those who have thin flesh, and clear pores:
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	It is necessary to strike only once, and it is necessary to make wide incisions, and somewhat deep;
et suce legierement.	and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to strike twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	the first time to open the pathway for thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to strike a third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	and when we want to let blood little by little, we strike only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we lose a lot of blood, we often replenish it;
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and if the blood is thick, pierce it forcefully, and ensure that the incision is such that the heart perceives it suddenly, and for those who have thick and hard skin and small pores, you should anoint the wounds with oil that is stimulating and dispersing:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is available, use violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or cucumber seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in spring, use watercress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess substances are thick and cold, use bitter oil, or balsam oil, or anise oil, and similar.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the person being treated has tender flesh and large pores, no oil should be applied, but after the suction, they should be washed with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or cucumber water, or porcelain berry water, or similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, let them rise from a decoction of myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.
