Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have large excesses should rise from old wine, or juice of suc (honey water), or a decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar ones;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	And it is not appropriate to use cupping before a bath or in a bath, but after the bath for one hour or two;
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And do not let them sleep after cupping, and it is necessary for them to walk around when they should be cupped and when they have been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And be wary if the person who is being treated is choleric, and if the blood is too thin and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	then it is necessary for them to take cold things, such as pomegranates and endive and lettuce grown in the shade, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and drink pigeon soup, and eat turtle meat, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold constitution should take syrup of honey, and fragrant wine that is between old and new, and eat porridge, and eat thrushes and small birds and pigeons;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and on the day that he will be bled, he should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and one should give some men occasionally trocar or nutmeg before bleeding, or after, to comfort the main limbs;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and let the blood be thin, but it is not appropriate for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The cupping glasses that are applied without cutting are those placed over the liver, and over the spleen, and for gout, and on the abdomen and buttocks and thighs and hip, because these members do not tolerate cutting, and we only use them to draw blood from one part of the body to another, as we place them on the breasts when a child is sick;
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	To remove the viscosity which is in the limb, as we place suction cups on the abdomen and on the neck to reduce the swelling of the limb;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and it removes the pain when there is an obstruction or stone, and by its attractive power it may remove the obstruction, or dislodge the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	and it does this when applied to the liver and spleen when there is retained wind, and these suction cups are administered empty to suck only;
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	and sometimes they are administered together with heat, and at other times filled with hot water, as in cases of pleurisy, and in such a manner that the suction cup is filled with warm water alone, or with water in which suitable herbs have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping vessel administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And let it be two fingers wide and half a palm long, and let there be a small hole in the center, as for threading a needle, and it should be of iron, underneath so that it does not scratch the patient when placed on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and let there be across the center an iron or steel bar, to hold a candle securely, and let there be both large and small ones according to the illnesses and age of those who use them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the suction cups for children are different from those for the elderly, and for the thin compared to the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one should place this suction cup on the limb as follows:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	Take the candle of wax or linen, and place it inside the cupping vessel across from the shaft that is in the cupping vessel, so that the flame is at the bottom of the cupping vessel so it does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the limb, and hold your two fingers over the opening we mentioned, so that when you want to, the steam goes out, and then remove the cupping vessel;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and apply the dressing as before, and repeat it often if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the cupping vessel used for treating pleurisy, there is no shaft or opening, and it is not applied except when it is full of fluid, and it is placed on the limb solely for that purpose;
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Sandwiches are not applied except to members where cups cannot be placed due to their small size, such as the lips and gums, and similar places;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and on bare flesh areas such as the back or buttocks, and other similar places;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the use is that when you find sandwiches in mild conditions that are clear and suitable for treatment, take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and place them in mild water until they become accustomed, and have nothing in their stomachs;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then bleed and cup the affected area, then rub the limb until it turns red, and apply the sandwiches;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full, and fall off, if it is a place where one can apply cups, then apply them, for this is very useful afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, then lift the area with ease, and then with water, very well, and then apply pressure;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the swelling persists near the veins, moisten a cloth of linen in cold water and apply it, until the vein is relieved;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the vein is swollen, then apply powdered vitriol, or gall nuts, and similar things, until it is relieved;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	and you place half of peeled beans on the area, and leave them until they heat up in that spot, it will now be alleviated;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	And if you need more, take other veins.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the veins do not want to be taken, rub the place with fresh blood, or insert a needle until the blood flows, and then apply them, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will harden;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they fall off, sprinkle a bit of aloes and frankincense powder, or ash, so they will now adhere.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine and deals with the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Beware, foolish physician, that they throw themselves into this chapter, having never read any ancient books or letters about it;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason the science is strange in our land, because I have never found any good one;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing of it except through the knowledge of ancient books, in which I have studied so much that I have acquired understanding, and by experience, and by the habit of my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	and I have described for you in this chapter what is contained within it, and I have summarized at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are mentioned, as I have done in these two preceding chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say in the prologue of this book the main points of discourse and the chapters where the wise one applies his understanding, and remains on the truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or torsion or sprain occurs to someone, you must hurry to treat the patient from both sides if nothing prevents it, such as weakness of body, children, or elderly;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or if the time is not very warm, or too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	And eat cold things, that is to say cold joints, and meat of birds and kids, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill yourself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have no fear of a hot abscess or spreading matter in the limb;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	If the patient returns to a better condition than he had used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that promote thick and sticky healing, such as boiled wheat in water, rice, headcheese, feet, pork belly, eggs, fresh fish, strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For such nourishment promotes healing and the broken bones heal more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones broken of old and infirm people cannot be well set or mended according to their nature due to the dryness of the limbs, nor can those who are too tender, such as the bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but do not worry, reset the broken bone with thick bandages that hold and join the limb together, until it strengthens as it was before;
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And do not exhaust him of his strength, and for this reason it is necessary to feed him on coarse meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the hip, or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all manners of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes along the grain, and another across it, like the shaft of a writing quill.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with just a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And for each method, let there be its own instrument, and its proper equipment in the restoration, according to what memory brings forth.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and the fracture of the bone is known by the fact that the limb is twisted, and it is clearly apparent by its displacement, and sounds hollow to the touch.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twisting or sound upon pressing, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no fracture.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it may still have twisting, or cracking, or small fractures.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not necessary to move it by hand, but apply the medicines that follow hereafter, and then gently press it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And you should know that for the fracture that goes into the marrow, and where the two parts are dislocated, they must now be set evenly so that healing splints may be applied.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if healing splints are applied, leave them on for some days until the swelling is reduced.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then place it evenly to the mold that you can gently and wisely, and know that the restoration of this is easier than that where there are fragments.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then secure it as needed subsequently.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if the bone is fractured into pieces, bind it from two parts, whether it is an arm or leg, or with your hand for smaller members, or with two bands, or with one band and your hand.
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	And place the limb according to its natural form, so that when the parts of the broken member are separated, reset all the fragments in their places as much as you can, and ensure that your work does not cause injury or pain to the patient;
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And properly align the two ends of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And feel it well with your hand if it seems to you that it is not right:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	if you set it properly, and do not pull it too tightly, nor press so much as those who cause heat and contraction in the limb through their work, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is properly set, instruct the patient well not to move it, neither while awake nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and ensure carefully that the limb is so secure that it does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when it feels any pain, it is not properly set, and it must be placed in such a position that it does not feel any pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and ensure that it is placed correctly so that no curvature occurs when it is restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken limb is according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small limbs, such as arms and thumbs and similar:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	it is necessary to wrap them in soft and fine linen cloths;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those who are thick, such as thigh and leg:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	it is necessary to wrap with a wide and hard bandage, for the wide straps embrace the entire large limb, and compress it equally from all sides, so there are no gaps;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then tie around light rollers, three times or four according to the limb, and press your hand slightly on the entire bandage, then go above the break and compress it less so that the break can move a little;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and gradually loosen the bandage little by little until you cover most of the healthy area, then take another bandage and wrap it again above the broken area;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then return to the part on the side of the fracture and compress it moderately, not too strongly nor too weakly, as we have said in the first chapter above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then place linen or cloths between the bandages so that they are all even, then wrap everything with a bandage, and then put your well-made splints on if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, place hot poultices that reduce the abscess and alleviate the swelling, and leave it like this for several days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then bind over your splints, and they should be half the width of a palm, made carefully from hazelwood or the wood used for skewers, or palm ribs, and should follow this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the splint which one places on the fracture be a little larger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and it should be as long as is necessary for the limb, whether small or large;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then press against the splints as you did in the first hour, then bind it with bandages, just as on the fracture in the first hour;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	tighter above, looser below;
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and the bandages should be medium thickness, not too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the bandages are too thick, as I have seen in the works of fools who use twisted linen cords for their bindings, and this is a great error, because the binding cannot be even if it is too fine, and it should not have less than two fingers' width between each splint.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is pierced by the points of the stars after being bound in their beds, place below them linen plugs, or wool rags, so that they do not become entangled.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the splinter, and the skin is broken, I will describe the treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And you should know that it is not appropriate to extract all the splinters from broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limb is large, one should not put on splints before five days or seven, or more according to your experience with a hot abscess ensuing.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	and see here the method of ancient plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and take flour that is kept near the mill walls, and mix it abundantly with eggs, and apply this preparation, not too thick or too thin, and use it, and this is the common method of a plaster restoring fractures in many cases, especially for women and children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another method of a plaster restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Take ten drams of aloes wood and styrax and anise and spikenard and gum arabic and mastic, mix them together.
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	Take five drams of myrrh and aloes.
alechil VIIII З.;	Take nine drams of alecost.
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	and make it into powder, and mix it with the yolk of an egg;
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	If the person's constitution is hot, use this plaster, for it is well composed, and quickly restores broken bones, and benefits many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another method of plaster for treating sprains:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	Take mugwort and viper's bugloss, one handful each;
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	take myrrh and aloes, one pound each;
acaice VI З.;	take acetum, six pounds;
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	take Armenian bole ten pounds, and grind well, and mix with water or egg white, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another method for plasters for joints and bones out of place, to alleviate the pain that occurs, and for wear on the bone, and fractures:
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	take new wool, and boil it in lard and oil, and apply to the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not heal, but it is good for soothing hot abscesses and properly alleviates the pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another way of applying a plaster to restore broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	take dried mulberry leaves and herb leaves, and grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of plaster for the restoration of a broken bone and to reduce the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take root of mallows, chamomile, violets flowers, flour of oats, of each one part;
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	and grind, and mix with wine, and if the limb is heated, mix it with moist coriander water, or just water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to make a plaster stronger than the first one, when a hard abscess comes during the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take roots of mallows, and seeds of flax, almond, honey locust, and spurge, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of each one part;
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	and grind, and mix with salt water, or fresh water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates states in his book that one should not place anything on a broken limb to restore strength except for plaster made of wax and oil, and nothing more, and he says it should be neither too hard nor too soft.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And Galen seems to suggest that for a broken limb, one should place dry and slightly warm things on it to restore strength, such as myrrh, aloes, and incense, and similar items, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another method of plaster for injury and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	take mutton and human fat, or bird feathers, and vervain, and mix equally, and grind them, and make a plaster and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then loosen it a little after, and be careful if the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved from its place;
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	do not loosen it by hand for days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hurry, and loosen it, and remove the plaster now;
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	and take a light cloth, and a sponge soaked in sea water, and dip it in water, and apply it to the area until the itching stops, and the pain is relieved;
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the limb rest for an hour, then place dry wool soaked in water or rose oil on it, and bind it with a bandage until you are sure of a hot abscess;
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and reduce the inflammation of the limb, and remove the pain, then restart the gentle treatment, and a little plaster, and do not strain it as strongly as before;
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and gently until he is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is red and swollen and painful and inflamed are gone from all over, and you need ointment and linen, then restart it as you did first equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if the limb shows no sign of what we have said, do not dislocate it before three days or four or five or seven.
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	and sometimes leave it for twenty days, depending on what is observed, until the break heals, and the bones come closer together.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	then restrain it more than before, and increase its flesh, as I said before;
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and if you see the area dry more than necessary, know that no new flesh can come there;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	then apply warm water compresses every time you dislocate it, and do this every third day, and loosen the bandage a little;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	By this work then correct the nourishment to the limb, and quickly mend what those foolish doctors do, who abruptly reset the limb:
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	It is wrong, and such work is fearful, and I see nothing else but to leave it and do it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various ways of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many kinds of fractures, and diverse shapes, and the causes are distinct;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	for there are fractures caused by the impact of a sword, and the force removes all the bone up to the surface beneath it, as if splitting wood or a staff;
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	and for this reason this kind of fracture is called a "splitting" or "chopping.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	When the sword strikes the bone from above without piercing it, and this manner of fracture is called "absolute";
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	and the wound from these two fractures is large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded impact, or split by the neck of a stone, or falling on a stone, or other similar circumstances.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a break that approaches the membrane beneath the bone, whether it is on top of the bone or near it, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And there is a wound that is set in the bone as fine as a hair, and this crack is small, and for this reason it is called a "hairline" fracture;
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	and there is a wound made by being hit by a stone, or by falling, or similar things, which causes a bone fragment to enter below, and the place is covered with hair as blacksmiths do when they hammer on their forge;
si entre li piere dedens.	and a stone enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more often to those who have soft bones in their head, such as children's heads;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and in all these types of fractures, small fragments may become displaced as they do;
et je em parlerai en son leu.	and I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we recognize all manners of fractures by the depression above them, and by probing with probes, and by the corrupted flesh that is on them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair-like appearance is recognized when, after uncovering the bone, one rubs along it, and the fracture appears clearly black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, be wary of any adverse effects on the patient, and if you see any bad signs, such as vomiting of bile, loss of consciousness, convulsions, paralysis, fever, and the eyes protruding and reddening, and other similar conditions in many circumstances, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any alarming signs, and you hope for recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wounded person first comes to you, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day so that you can do so.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the skin under the bone does not rot, and the accidents we have mentioned do not occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the fracture of the bone reaches the membrane that covers the brain, then you must split the affected part as follows:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and it is that you take the head of the patient carefully, and expose the bone in all ways that you can, and around the shape of the wound as deeply as you can, and if blood vessels bleed upon exposing the bone, or an abscess forms, use appropriate assistance, and fill the area with cloths soaked in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and allow the wound to rest until the swelling subsides, and be assured of no further bleeding;
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	then begin to remove around the bone, and this is done according to two methods of work:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	one method is that you cut closely around the incision, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make the second cut larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second method is that you have various incisions, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed, and made of iron.
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and work gently so that you do not bleed the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is hard and protruding, it is necessary that you pierce around it, thus administering incisions with files, not deeply enough to penetrate further into the skull bone, and it should have above the tip a margin or circle, so that the point does not pass beyond the bone;
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	And you must have several of them, so that each comes in its place according to the thickness of the bone, so that you have splinters for all parts of the head;
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And this is the form of the three kinds of splinters:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	To pierce around a broken bone, place one splinter on the bone and turn it until you know that the bone is pierced;
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	then place the splinter slightly further along, and do this all around, then cut with your incising tools the space of the bone that is between the holes, and do this as carefully and gently as we have said, until you draw out the bone either by hand or with any of the instruments you have such as forceps, pincers;
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	And guard that you do not touch the brain or the cerebellum.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced the bone, and drawn it out, then you must use an instrument that is prepared from the bone to all other similar instruments, resembling a scalpel, but it must be thinner and more delicate than other scalpels;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	and if anything remains of the small bones or any scales, then remove them gently with the instruments;
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	then treat the wound with dressings and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And the other method of work is that which Galen described, which is more skillful;
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and he praises it very much, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first to expose a part of the bone where the fracture opens up, so that when you have uncovered this part, you place below the head of this chisel, which has this shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut from one side, and the part to be cut is arched on both sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone;
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	then tap lightly with a small mallet on top, so that you gently cut around the bone all around, and take great care of the skin below;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is adhered to the bone, remove it gently, for it must be removed without harm, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not pierce through to the membrane, and the bone is broken only slightly from above, with small pieces present, then it is necessary behind that roughness, to remove the scales with a fine scraper which you must have in various quantities, to administer at each place what is most suitable, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Start with large scrapers and then use finer ones, and do not stop using them until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each of the other hair-like incisions and subtle fractures, you must manage them according to their direction;
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	And it is something that is not answered by one who has devoted his study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is uncovered, then you should take a piece of linen, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it on the wound;
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	then take another piece of doubled linen, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first layer of linen;
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	and apply this as lightly as you can so that you do not burden the wound, then administer another layer over it, and do not pull it too tight but just enough to cover the wound;
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and leave it thus for one or two days until the swelling is reduced, then release it, and administer medicines such as root of lily, and flour of vetches, and powder of incense, and aristology, and similar things;
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and from these things make powder, and apply it to the wound, and immediately administer cleansing medicines without caustic substances;
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and ensure that the wound is immediately clean, do not leave any ointment on it, nor allow pus to accumulate, because when pus accumulates on the cloth of the brain, it can lead to corruption and putrefaction, causing great harm to the patient;
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	for when something caustic is applied to the surface, it must be covered with another layer.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, take care if any harmful accidents happen to the patient, as we have said, it is uncertain without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if blackness comes not from anything other than the medicine that you have put on it, then you should take one part of honey and three parts of rose oil and add a little glue, and apply this mixture to it.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it according to the appropriate methods until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Know that sometimes the two parts of the skull above can be broken, or just one part, because these are two bones;
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	and the one below is made of cartilage and does not break, but can be pushed out of place or twisted, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, you should insert your small finger into the opening of the skull, and align that fracture with your finger inside, and outside with a pad, until the skull returns to its natural shape;
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And do this gently, and watch that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the nose, and your rod cannot reach that place, then you must place it equally on top of a slightly thickened rail.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is in two parts, then do likewise, and hurry to restore it on the first day, if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	unless, after the seventh or tenth day, when the swelling has subsided, then apply to the head of the neck cloths of linen if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	And you apply another on the other side, if the fracture is there;
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and let the cloths be thick enough to fill the openings of the neck.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some practitioners say that the tents should be moistened with butter, and changed each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It does not seem right to me, but they must be moistened in a mixture of egg whites and flour powder;
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	then leave it covered until the bone is hard and the cartilage is hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And sometimes one inserts goose feathers instead of bandages, and if there is a small cloth around it, it holds the dressing, and the patient blows through them;
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	or do as you wish.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if pus comes from abscesses in the nose while you are treating them, apply cerate or cotton moistened in rose oil, or a little bit of myrrh.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if pus does not come out, apply a plaster from the outside made of sesamum flour and powdered incense, mixed with egg whites, then put on light plugs, and do not bind the nose;
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the fracture of the nose is small, and it is broken into small pieces, then extract with suitable instruments, then sew the wound, and treat flesh wounds, and sealing, such as plasters and suitable ointments;
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound inside the nose, then treat it with tampons, and place strips of cloth, until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is fractured from the side, and there is no wound to exit, and the fracture is only inside, not broken into two parts but rather cracked internally, one can easily recognize it.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, that you place your index finger in the patient's mouth;
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	and if the fracture is on the left jawbone, then place your index finger of the right hand, and gently push the fracture inwards, and support it with the other hand from outside, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jaw fracture is displaced in two parts, you must administer an extension to both sides until they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if the movement or fracture of the teeth occurs, hold them with a gold, silver, or silk thread, then place wax on the broken jaw, and put on two cloths;
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	and place on the cloth a large splint well made, or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the jaw, and secure it as much as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the face changes shape, then loosen it on the third day, and then adjust what has changed.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	and apply a plaster on top, made from powder of the mill with plenty of egg or sesame flour, after you have removed the wax.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	and put on a poultice of light wool, and if the poultices adhere, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until they are healed;
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	many times it is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if large abscesses come, then treat them as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is both a fracture and a wound, check if any piece of the bone has been removed;
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	and carefully remove it with appropriate instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then widen it with flame according to your necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and none remain, then stitch the wound if it is wide, and apply suitable plasters to it, to promote flesh growth until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the strength
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The collarbone is often fractured multiple times near the shoulder, and the fracture occurs in three ways:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	where it is broken and separated into two pieces, with fragments, and this is the easiest to restore;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	Where there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the work is such that when there is a fracture without a wound, you should have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder where the bone is broken;
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other extends the arm towards the part.
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	Then place the fracture between your hands so that its form is as it should be, and there is no appearance or sign of displacement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you need to extend further, place under the patient's shoulder a round ball of cloth, or wool, and let it be as thick as necessary;
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and extend and lift the limb, and hold the ball with your hand so that you can place the fracture evenly as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the humerus out due to its position, then the patient should lie on their side and place a medium-sized pillow under the armpit, and have the assistant push down on the shoulder until the bone of the humerus is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	And then align the fracture with your hands, and if you find it shattered, you must cut into it;
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and gently pull the pieces apart, and if the bone cannot join due to any prominence, cut it with one of your incisors;
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but place the forceps away from this instrument to protect the surface;
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and it appears like a spoon, and is not jagged, and should be as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work;
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and it should have two heads, as you see, and one wide, and the other narrow, like the outline of the wound you made when you treated the bones;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are sure of a hot abscess, cut the wound open, and if the rupture is small, or you doubt it being a hot abscess, cover the wound with cloths and tents according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if abscesses come, wet the cloth in rose oil and honey and vinegar, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The binding of the bone, when it is without wounds and without cutting, is that you put on the bone a plaster made from powder from the mill and an egg white, and place light dressings over it, and place a pad under the splint if you need to.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	Then take a very wide bandage one palm wide, then place a double cloth over the dressings, and the plaster.
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a slender stick three digits wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage, so that the ends of the bandage hang down.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	and place the splint on the fracture, and wrap the bandage around the neck, and under the healthy shoulder blade, and under the affected shoulder blade;
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and realign each part, and when you see that the ligaments hold the fracture in place, and clearly see that the splint does not move off the broken bone, then examine it every day, and when the ligaments loosen, restrain them;
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	and have the patient lie on their back, and place a small pillow under the shoulder blade while they sleep, to lift the shoulder up;
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	this will ease the fracture of the collarbone by lifting the shoulder, where you bind the arm to the neck, and do not undo it unless a bad accident occurs, until twenty days;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	Then reapply the plaster if you see that it is necessary, and bind it in this way until it is restored.
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and it is restored within twenty-eight days, and in fewer days for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the fracture of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	It often happens that the shoulder is broken either widely or in the middle, and one can only know this by touching it.
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	treat it according to the shape of the break and reset it according to its natural form in all ways that you can.
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	then place powder from the mill with an abundance of egg, and light bandages, and put on one double layer of cloth.
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	Then place a splint wide and thin, a bit wider than the shoulder, and if the splint presses on any part of the shoulder, pad that area with linen cotton so that the splint rests evenly;
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	and then tightly secure it with a large bandage so that the splint does not move from its place, and check the binding each day;
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	and each time it loosens, tighten it again, and adjust the splint if it has moved from its place, and have the patient lie on their side;
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	and the shoulder should be immobilized for twenty or twenty-five days.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when this number of days is completed, then release it, and be careful, for it is not bone that will return to place easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes and points away from the heart, they cut it off, and do as we have said in the fracture of the collarbone to ease a hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely;
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it often breaks at the ends.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it inclines to one side, and the patient feels great pain, and lacks appetite, and sweats, and perhaps vomits blood, and the movement of the bones can be felt clearly through the skin.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is as follows: the patient lies on their back, and a cushion is placed between the shoulders, then press the shoulders, and bring together the ribs of both sides with your hands, and gently align in all ways possible, until the shape of the bone is as it should be;
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	then apply plasters and wads of fine salt, or some other light material, and wrap it in a cloth, securing it over the broken bone so that it does not move;
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	and turn the bandage tightly to the back, and tighten it gradually, and check each hour the bandage, and if it loosens, then tighten it;
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	and if it is necessary to loosen it for corrosion or itching that comes in the area, or pain or abscess, then hurry and loosen it, and remove the plaster, and address whatever has come from methods of treatment;
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	then reapply the plaster, and tighten it until it is secure.
de la brisure des costes	Of the fracture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Know that the breakage of ribs comes rarely except from heavy blows to the back, and at the front towards the chest, and they do not bend easily because they are slippery;
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and one feels well at the inquiry of both.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is such that you place it equal to the fracture, as is necessary.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and bind it with a splint if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the fracture of the ribs is inwardly displaced, the patient feels great pain and stabbing, as with pneumonia, because the bone pierces the tissue;
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and he coughs up blood clots, and vomits a lot of blood, and this is a serious condition, and the elderly are more prone to it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And there are those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that swell the belly, to push out the bruise from within.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this so that abscesses do not occur there if they have not already come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have occurred, then heal them.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And some say to place suction cups over the area, to draw out forcefully, and this seems reasonable;
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	still, there is concern that the suction cups may not draw out the excesses to the site due to the condition of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some say to cover the area with wool soaked in hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to make the application even around, then proceed with the treatment for pleurisy, of food and medication.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear from the bone piercing the tissue, and there is doubt for the patient, then it is necessary to cut into the area of the broken rib, and it is necessary to place an instrument underneath to protect the surface.
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then one must cut the bone, and gently pull it apart, and then sew together the two edges of the wound if it is large, and treat it with plasters until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if small abscesses come, place cloths soaked in rose oil on the area.
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat the area as needed for the abscess, and let them lie on their side where it is necessary, until they are healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the fracture of the neck (or collarbone)
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	Sometimes there is a fracture of the neck bones, and it can happen that they bend;
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and also to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be well or not, observe if you see their hands softened and swollen and dead, and cannot move or stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many conditions, and if they move and feel well when they are pinched and pricked, know that the joint of the bone is safe, and that the patient can be treated, if proper care is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if a similar thing happens to the spine of the back, and you wish to know whether it is sound or not, observe if the feet are weakened, and if the symptoms that indicate paralysis are present, and on the back there is swelling and involuntary evacuation;
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	and when it has been pressed upon its abdomen, there is involuntary evacuation.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is lying on his back and wishes to sit up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Know that it is deadly:
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	do not attempt to treat it.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these accidents do not occur to him, then the matter is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the treatment is that you should apply heat if there is a hot abscess, and place on the spine rose oil or egg yolk oil until it subsides;
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	then apply one of the comforting and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest;
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	and let him not sleep on that part where he feels the pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if any bone breaks, it must be set immediately;
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and remove the bone, then sew together the two edges of the wound if it is large, and treat it with an ointment that promotes flesh growth until he is healed;
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	And if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the humerus," place your thumb from your left hand inside it as far as possible, then equal to the other hand's power, then apply the poultice and the bandage if you need them;
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then compress it, and if there are displaced bones, cut them out, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	It sometimes happens that the hip bone is broken, and if it does happen, there should be a slight reduction in the head.
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	And it extends long, and inclines inward, causing the patient pain at the site, and swelling where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the restoration is such that you extend your hand upon it, until you are on the fracture;
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and feel where the fracture is and its shape;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	and if the fracture is only at the head, then set it equally so that it has a natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is lengthwise, where it inclines inward, make the patient lie on their stomach until the restoration of that fracture is prepared.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have set it equal, then apply a poultice, then place a stick or board over it and bind the fracture so that it does not move;
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and pad the area under the ribs until the sides are even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if swelling comes, do not touch it, until the swelling is reduced, and then apply what we have said before;
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	and then return to the restoration, and compress it as is appropriate, if there is no harmful incident;
et c’est li maniere.	and this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the fracture of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The shoulder joint is what is between the collarbone and the head of the shoulder, and if it is dislocated, it should be restored according to one of the two methods:
